## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / nonlinear dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of state variables x (position), v (velocity), and possibly explicit time t, which matches second-order ODE models for (non)linear oscillators. Typical relationships combine restoring forces depending on x (often nonlinear), damping terms depending on v (linear or nonlinear), and optional external forcing depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator (Hooke restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude conservative oscillation)
- Linear viscous damping + Hooke restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (external periodic forcing)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / Mathieu-type)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Softening with quintic correction: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (higher-order restoring nonlinearity)
- Pendulum equation (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle pendulum; x as angle)
- Nonlinear (velocity-squared) drag: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic/quadratic damping)
- Rayleigh damping (self-excited): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (negative damping at small v, positive at large v)
- van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping producing limit cycles)
- LiÃ©nard-type oscillator (general nonlinear damping + restoring): dv_dt = -g(x) - f(x) * v where g(x)=c0*x+c1*x**3 and f(x)=c2+c3*x**2 (broad class including many self-oscillators)
- Conservative oscillator from potential gradient: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (force derived from polynomial potential; no damping/forcing)
- Piecewise linear spring (dead-zone/backlash proxy): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Max(Abs(x) - c2, 0) * Sign(x) - c3 * v (stiffness changes beyond a gap/threshold)
- State-dependent frequency (amplitude-dependent stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x**2) * x - c2 * v (equivalent to cubic stiffness written as variable stiffness)
- Non-autonomous forcing with harmonics: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (multi-tone driving / Fourier forcing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force â†’ dv_dt depends on x only and is typically an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x - x**3), reflecting symmetry of the potential about x=0.
- Energy dissipation â†’ terms proportional to v (or v*Abs(v), v**3) should reduce mechanical energy, so their sign typically opposes v (negative damping contribution).
- Self-excited oscillations / limit cycles â†’ damping that changes sign with amplitude (e.g., (c0 - c1*x**2)*v or (c0 - c1*v**2)*v) produces growth at small amplitude and saturation at large amplitude.
- Geometric nonlinearity in rotational systems â†’ sin(c*x) restoring indicates angle-like x and yields amplitude-dependent period/frequency.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness â†’ +x**3 term inside restoring (i.e., dv_dt includes -x - x**3) hardens; dv_dt includes -x + x**3 softens, changing frequency with amplitude.
- External periodic driving â†’ additive sin(c*t+phi) terms can create resonance, beats, and steady-state oscillations; multiple harmonics suggest non-sinusoidal forcing.
- Parametric excitation â†’ stiffness multiplied by cos(c*t) (i.e., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) indicates Mathieu-type instability regions rather than direct forcing.
- Dry friction / backlash approximations â†’ Sign(x) or Sign(v), Max(Abs(x)-c,0), and other nonsmooth terms indicate stick-slip or piecewise stiffness/damping behavior.
- State-dependent damping â†’ factors like (c0 + c1*x**2)*v suggest damping increases with displacement (e.g., aerodynamic or geometric effects in mechanisms).
